      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence complex

          across different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is
          critical for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association
          studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes in
          disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
          architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
          play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait

          latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation is

      response:
        output: ' Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, making it crucial to understand how they influence complex traits. Gaining insight into expression regulation across different conditions is vital for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped reveal the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms; however, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions significantly contribute to disease origins and progression. To address these gaps, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis, utilizing modules of genes with similar expression patterns across shared conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and uncovers mechanisms of action. In addition, using CRISPR screen to examine lipid regulation, we find functionally important players that lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. This framework reveals potential targets missed by single-gene strategies and provides a novel way to interpret genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, thus contextualizing their impact on disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/phenoplier/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: ' Genes work together in specific contexts to carry out their functions, influencing the development of complex traits. To understand how genes contribute to these traits, we need a deeper understanding of gene expression regulation under different conditions. This insight is crucial for discovering new therapeutic approaches. Transcriptome-wide association studies have been helpful in determining the roles of individual genes in disease mechanisms. However, models predict that gene-gene interactions play key roles in the origin and progression of diseases. We developed PhenoPLIER, a computational approach to map gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on gene modules with similar expression patterns across conditions. Our findings reveal that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to examine lipid regulation, we observe that important functional players lack associations but are prioritized within trait-associated gene modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER offers an innovative approach for contextualizing genetic associations and potentially uncovers overlooked therapeutic targets. This novel framework provides a new perspective on interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.'

      response:
        output: ' Genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions, necessitating the elucidation of how they influence complex traits. The comprehension of gene expression regulation across different conditions is crucial for understanding disease mechanisms and developing effective treatments. Transcriptome-wide association studies have allowed us to recognize the role of individual genes in relation to relevant disease processes; however, contemporary models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal part in the onset and progression of diseases. PhenoPLIER is an innovative computational approach designed to map gene-trait associations with pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This approach is based on modules containing genes expressing similar patterns across different conditions, which are fundamental for understanding how specific diseases are associated with certain cell types'' gene expressions. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairings and mechanisms of action. In a CRISPR screen, we discovered functionally important players not previously linked to traits, but prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Conclusively, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets often missed by single-gene strategies. In doing so, PhenoPLIER presents a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.'

        output: ' Genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions, and understanding how they influence complex traits requires examining expression regulation under various conditions. This knowledge is crucial for developing new therapies that target these mechanisms. Current transcriptome-wide association studies reveal the role of individual genes in disease-relevant processes. However, modern models emphasize gene-gene interactions in determining disease origin and progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that utilizes modules based on genes with similar expression patterns across conditions to map gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data for joint analysis. Our findings demonstrate significant associations between diseases and relevant cell types'' gene modules, and accurate predictions of known drug-disease pairs and the mechanisms of action. In addition, a CRISPR screen on lipid regulation supports this methodology by identifying functionally important genes without individual association but prioritized within trait-associated gene modules. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER incorporates gene expression patterns to contextualize genetic associations, revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies and provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.'

      response:
        output: ' Genes collaborate to carry out their functions in specific contexts, necessitating an understanding of how they influence complex traits. Unveiling gene expression regulation across various conditions is crucial for unraveling the mechanisms behind diseases and developing effective therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on individual genes'' roles in disease-related processes, modern models anticipate that interactions among multiple genes play a vital role in determining the origin and progression of complex traits. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational tool designed to map gene-trait associations alongside pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is built on modules of co-expressed genes sharing similar expression patterns across various conditions. By doing so, we observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs while unveiling their mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we found functionally important players lacking direct associations, yet prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, this approach incorporates gene expression patterns and reveals potential drug targets missed by single-gene approaches, ultimately providing a framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.'

This knowledge is crucial for developing new therapies as it reveals disease-relevant mechanisms. While transcriptome-wide association studies have contributed to understanding the role of individual genes in diseases, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a significant part in the origin and progression of complex traits. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. In conclusion, this approach integrates gene co-expression to contextualize genetic associations and potentially reveals therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies.           to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in

          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their functions, making understanding their effects on complex traits crucial for developing therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have shown the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms. However, modern models suggest gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER''s representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across various conditions. The approach demonstrates that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types and accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs, along with their mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation reveals functionally important players without strong gene associations but prioritized by PhenoPLIER when part of trait-associated modules. In conclusion, by incorporating co-expressed gene groups, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations and identifies overlooked therapeutic targets, providing a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through gene module analysis.'

          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in

          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

By employing CRISPR screening on lipid regulation, we found that functionally important players not associated with any gene but are part of trait-associated gene groups when analyzed using the PhenoPLIER method. This approach offers a new perspective for interpreting genetic associations based on co-expressed genes, highlighting potential targets missed by single-gene approaches. Thus, PhenoPLIER provides an innovative framework to comprehend genetic links through the lens of gene modules and enhance disease etiology understanding and drug mechanisms exploration.'

          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

Gaining insight into how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a deep understanding of expression regulation across various conditions, which is crucial for developing new treatments. Transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in unveiling the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms; however, contemporary models predict that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in the genesis and progression of complex diseases. To this end, we introduce PhenoPLIER, an innovative computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules comprising genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and decodes mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to study lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.'

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene

          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that

          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

Gaining insight into expression regulation across different conditions is vital for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped reveal the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms; however, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions significantly contribute to disease origins and progression. To address these gaps, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis, utilizing modules of genes with similar expression patterns across shared conditions.             text: ' Genes collaborate to carry out their functions in specific contexts, necessitating an understanding of how they influence complex traits. Unveiling gene expression regulation across various conditions is crucial for unraveling the mechanisms behind diseases and developing effective therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on individual genes'' roles in disease-related processes, modern models anticipate that interactions among multiple genes play a vital role in determining the origin and progression of complex traits. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational tool designed to map gene-trait associations alongside pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is built on modules of co-expressed genes sharing similar expression patterns across various conditions. By doing so, we observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs while unveiling their mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we found functionally important players lacking direct associations, yet prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, this approach incorporates gene expression patterns and reveals potential drug targets missed by single-gene approaches, ultimately providing a framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.'

Comprehending how these genes influence complex traits necessitates understanding the regulation of expression across various conditions, which is crucial for developing novel therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed individual gene roles in disease mechanisms, modern architectural models predict that gene-gene interactions play a vital role in disease etiology and progression. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach for analyzing gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation. This representation is based on gene modules with similar expression patterns across conditions. Furthermore, through a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation, we observe that functionally crucial players lack direct associations but are prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, by integrating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and expose potential targets missed through single-gene strategies. This novel framework enables the interpretation of genetic associations through a gene module lens, offering a comprehensive approach for studying disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

              Python code returned false

                "PhenoPLIER" not in output.split(".")[0]

              ---
               We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that combines gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. Genes collaborate in specific contexts to carry out their functions, necessitating understanding of expression regulation across different conditions to elucidate complex traits' etiologies. This insight is crucial for developing novel therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed individual gene roles in disease mechanisms, current models predict that gene-gene interactions play a vital role in the emergence and progression of diseases. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across specific conditions. We observe that diseases are strongly linked to gene modules expressed within relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and mechanisms of action. Additionally, employing a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation, we find essential players not directly associated but prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, incorporating co-expressed genes within PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations and unveils potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. This novel framework enables us to analyze genetic associations through the lens of gene expression patterns, thereby enhancing our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              ---
               We present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that combines gene-trait associations and pharmacological data into a unified latent representation for joint analysis. Genes operate together in specific contexts to perform their functions, necessitating an understanding of expression regulation across different conditions. This knowledge is crucial for developing effective therapies, as it sheds light on the influence of genes on complex traits. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover individual gene roles in disease mechanisms; however, modern models of complex trait architecture propose that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's approach is based on modules of co-expressed genes across similar conditions, revealing that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. We demonstrate the accuracy of our method in predicting known drug-disease pairs, inferring mechanisms of action, and identifying key players in complex traits using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations, revealing potential targets that might be missed by single-gene approaches. Thus, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, offering valuable insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              ---
               We present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that facilitates the integration of gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation. Genes interact in concert to carry out their functions within specific contexts; thus, understanding how these genes contribute to complex traits demands an investigation into expression regulation under diverse conditions. This knowledge is crucial for developing novel therapeutics. Transcriptome-wide association studies have significantly advanced our understanding of the individual roles of genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, current models of complex trait architecture propose that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease etiology and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes with similar expression patterns across various conditions. Our analysis shows that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, while our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates their mechanisms of action. Through a CRISPR screen of lipid regulation, we observed that functionally significant genes, lacking direct associations, were prioritized within trait-associated gene modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and identify potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies, thus providing a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

              ---
               To address the challenge of understanding complex traits, we introduce PhenoPLIER - a computational approach mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data to a shared latent representation for joint analysis. Genes collaborate within specific contexts to execute their functions, and comprehending how they influence complex traits necessitates the elucidation of expression regulation under different conditions. Transcriptome-wide association studies have uncovered genes' roles in disease mechanisms, but modern models suggest gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease etiology and progression. Our approach is based on modules of co-expressed genes across similar conditions, revealing significant associations between diseases and relevant cell types. Additionally, PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and deciphers their mechanisms of action, even prioritizing functionally important players not associated with individual genes but present in trait-associated gene modules. Thus, by considering groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can provide new perspectives on genetic associations, illuminating previously overlooked therapeutic targets and offering a novel framework to interpret genetic data through the lens of gene modules.

              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is

              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for

              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").

              ---
               We introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational method that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. To understand the influence of genes on complex traits, we must explore their interactions and functions in specific contexts. Transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms; however, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease etiology. By considering groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER enables the contextualization of genetic associations and reveals potential targets missed by single-gene approaches. Our method can identify gene modules associated with diseases and accurately predict known drug-disease pairs, highlighting their mechanisms of action. It prioritizes functionally important players that lack individual association but are enriched in trait-associated gene modules. Overall, PhenoPLIER offers a new framework for analyzing genetic associations through the lens of gene expression patterns, enhancing our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

Our study's results demonstrate that diseases have significant associations with gene modules expressed within relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs while uncovering their mechanisms of action. Through a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation, we identify that functionally important players lack associations yet are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, incorporating groups of co-expressed genes via PhenoPLIER enables contextualization of genetic associations and highlights potential targets missed through single-gene approaches. As a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, PhenoPLIER presents an innovative approach to understanding disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

            text: ' Genes work in concert with one another within specific contexts to execute their functions. Gaining insight into how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a deep understanding of expression regulation across various conditions, which is crucial for developing new treatments. Transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in unveiling the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms; however, contemporary models predict that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in the genesis and progression of complex diseases. To this end, we introduce PhenoPLIER, an innovative computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules comprising genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and decodes mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to study lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.'

              ---
               Genes work together in specific contexts to carry out their functions, influencing complex traits. To understand how these genes impact disease etiology and drug mechanisms, it is crucial to examine gene expression regulation across various conditions. While transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed individual gene roles in relevant disease mechanisms, modern models indicate that gene-gene interactions play a vital part in complex trait origins and progression. Here, we present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that bridges gene-trait associations with pharmacological perturbation data by mapping them into shared latent representation for joint analysis. Based on modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns across conditions, our method demonstrates significant disease associations to gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, effectively predicting known drug-disease pairs and shedding light on mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack direct associations but are prioritized within trait-associated gene modules by PhenoPLIER.

              ---
               Genes often function collaboratively in specific contexts to execute their roles. To grasp how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a mechanistic understanding of the regulation of gene expression across diverse scenarios. This knowledge is pivotal for developing new therapeutic approaches. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms. However, recent models anticipate that genetic interactions are instrumental to the origin and progression of diseases. To address this, we introduce PhenoPLIER – a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns across relevant conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in pertinent cell types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs as well as elucidates the mechanisms of action. Additionally, through a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation, we find that functionally significant players lack direct associations but are prioritized within trait-associated gene modules by PhenoPLIER.

              ---
               Genes interact with one another in specific contexts, contributing to their functional roles. A deeper understanding of how these genes influence complex traits necessitates an investigation into expression regulation across different conditions and its significance for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have highlighted the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in the etiology and progression of diseases. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation utilizes modules comprising genes with similar expression patterns across various conditions, which enables the identification of disease associations with relevant cell types. Our approach demonstrates accuracy in predicting known drug-disease pairs as well as deciphering mechanisms of action. Moreover, by conducting a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we observe that functionally important players lacking direct gene-trait associations are prioritized within the trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

               Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their functions, and understanding their influence on complex traits requires knowledge of how they regulate expression under different conditions. This insight is critical for developing new therapies. Although transcriptome-wide association studies reveal the roles of individual genes in disease mechanisms, modern models of complex trait architecture predict that gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. Transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in revealing the roles of individual genes in disease mechanisms.               etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
              functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
              repurposing, clustering of complex traits'. Revise the following
              abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure
              and follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits
              in a single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely
              necessary to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the
              abstract must follow the following structure: 1) The context must
              communicate to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first
              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is
              narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for
              distinguishing the paper’s contributions from the current state of
              the art by communicating what is missing in the literature (i.e.,
              the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e., the connection
              between the specific gap and the broader context that the paper
              opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question. Then
              you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
              Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the
              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").


              Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
              contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
              influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions. It has been
              shown that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.

            their functions. Determining how these genes influence complex

            critical for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide
            association studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes
            in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
            architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
            play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
            introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
            associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
            latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation is
            based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
            the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
            associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
            our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
            inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen
            to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
            players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
